			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Take-Two" redirects here. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Take_Two_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Take Two (disambiguation)">Take Two</a>.</div>

<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>
<p><b>Take-Two Interactive Software, Inc.</b> is an American video game <a href="/wiki/Holding_company" title="Holding company">holding company</a> based in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>. The company owns two major <a href="/wiki/Imprint_(trade_name)" title="Imprint (trade name)">publishing labels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rockstar_Games" title="Rockstar Games">Rockstar Games</a> and <a href="/wiki/2K_(company)" title="2K (company)">2K</a>, which operate internal <a href="/wiki/Video_game_developer" title="Video game developer">game development studios</a>. Take-Two's portfolio includes numerous successful video game series across personal computer and video game consoles, including <i><a href="/wiki/BioShock_(series)" title="BioShock (series)">BioShock</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Borderlands_(series)" title="Borderlands (series)">Borderlands</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Civilization_(series)" title="Civilization (series)">Civilization</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Grand_Theft_Auto" title="Grand Theft Auto">Grand Theft Auto</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/NBA_2K" title="NBA 2K">NBA 2K</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Red_Dead" title="Red Dead">Red Dead</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/XCOM" class="mw-redirect" title="XCOM">XCOM</a></i>. As of March 2018, it is the third-largest publicly traded game company in the Americas and Europe after <a href="/wiki/Activision_Blizzard" title="Activision Blizzard">Activision Blizzard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Arts" title="Electronic Arts">Electronic Arts</a>, with an estimated <a href="/wiki/Market_capitalization" title="Market capitalization">market cap</a> of <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$13 billion</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p><table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em"><caption class="fn src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Increase" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300"> 5,214<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> (2019)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><a href="/wiki/Subsidiary" title="Subsidiary">Subsidiaries</a></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><div class="plainlist"><ul><li><a href="/wiki/2K_(company)" title="2K (company)">2K</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Ghost_Story_Games" title="Ghost Story Games">Ghost Story Games</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/NBA_2K_League" title="NBA 2K League">NBA 2K League</a> (50%)</li><li><a href="/wiki/Private_Division" title="Private Division">Private Division</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Rockstar_Games" title="Rockstar Games">Rockstar Games</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Social_Point" class="mw-redirect" title="Social Point">Social Point</a></li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;">Website</th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.take2games.com/">take2games.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table><p>Take-Two was founded by Ryan Brant in September 1993, looking to become a major publisher in the video game area. The company went <a href="/wiki/Public_company" title="Public company">public</a> in April 1997, and later acquired the publisher and developer behind <i><a href="/wiki/Grand_Theft_Auto_(video_game)" title="Grand Theft Auto (video game)">Grand Theft Auto</a></i>, through which it formed Rockstar Games and <a href="/wiki/Rockstar_North" title="Rockstar North">Rockstar North</a>, respectively, and also leading to their long-standing "label" structure. From 2003 to 2005, the company fell under investigation by the <a href="/wiki/Security_and_Exchange_Commission" class="mw-redirect" title="Security and Exchange Commission">Security and Exchange Commission</a> related to corporate and personal financial fraud after going public that led to Brant resigning by 2006 alongside the departures of other former executives and board members. As a result of this mismanagement, the company's majority shareholders led a takeover of Take-Two in March 2007, replacing them with <a href="/wiki/Strauss_Zelnick" title="Strauss Zelnick">Strauss Zelnick</a> as the new Chairman and CEO. Take-Two subsequently rejected a <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$1.9 billion</span> buyout from <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Arts" title="Electronic Arts">Electronic Arts</a> in 2008. Since then, the company has continued to grow through acquisitions and creation of new studios. More recently, Take-Two created the label <a href="/wiki/Private_Division" title="Private Division">Private Division</a> to support publishing from <a href="/wiki/Independent_video_game_development" class="mw-redirect" title="Independent video game development">independent developers</a>, and acquired the developer <a href="/wiki/Social_Point" class="mw-redirect" title="Social Point">Social Point</a> to establish itself in the <a href="/wiki/Mobile_game" title="Mobile game">mobile game</a> market. The company also owns 50% of professional <a href="/wiki/ESports" class="mw-redirect" title="ESports">esports</a> organization <a href="/wiki/NBA_2K_League" title="NBA 2K League">NBA 2K League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046785">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-3 .toclevel-2 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-4 .toclevel-3 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-5 .toclevel-4 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-6 .toclevel-5 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-7 .toclevel-6 ul{display:none}</style><div class="toclimit-3"><div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none"><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Take-Two_Interactive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History" data-section="1" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="1993.E2.80.932000:_Formation_and_initial_growth"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1993–2000:_Formation_and_initial_growth">1993–2000: Formation and initial growth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Take-Two_Interactive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1993–2000: Formation and initial growth" data-section="2" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Take-Two Interactive was founded on September 30, 1993, by Ryan Brant, the son of <i><a href="/wiki/Interview_(magazine)" title="Interview (magazine)">Interview</a></i> co-owner <a href="/wiki/Peter_Brant" title="Peter Brant">Peter Brant</a>. While Brant had worked for his father on business matters for <i>Interview</i>, he wanted to forge his own path, deciding to create a video game publishing company. Brant stated "I wanted to get into a business where I could raise capital as a younger guy. In technology people expect you to be a younger person."<sup id="cite_ref-Histories_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Histories-5">[5]</a></sup> An initial <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$1.5 million</span> in funding was established from family and private investors to launch the company.<sup id="cite_ref-Histories_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Histories-5">[5]</a></sup></p><p>Starting with <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Crusader" title="Star Crusader">Star Crusader</a></i> in 1993, Take-Two found its first major success within games that included <a href="/wiki/Full_motion_video" title="Full motion video">full motion video</a> with well-known live actors performing the parts, following the success that Mechadeus had with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daedalus_Encounter" title="The Daedalus Encounter">The Daedalus Encounter</a></i> which featured <a href="/wiki/Tia_Carrere" title="Tia Carrere">Tia Carrere</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Histories_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Histories-5">[5]</a></sup> Take-Two hired <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Hopper" title="Dennis Hopper">Dennis Hopper</a>, among others, to star in parts for <i><a href="/wiki/Hell:_A_Cyberpunk_Thriller" title="Hell: A Cyberpunk Thriller">Hell: A Cyberpunk Thriller</a></i> (1994), which sold over 300,000 copies over the following year and established profit for the company. This was followed by <i><a href="/wiki/Ripper_(video_game)" title="Ripper (video game)">Ripper</a></i> (1996), of which <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$625,000</span> of its <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$2.5 million</span> budget was used to hire actors such as <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Walken" title="Christopher Walken">Christopher Walken</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karen_Allen" title="Karen Allen">Karen Allen</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Burgess_Meredith" title="Burgess Meredith">Burgess Meredith</a>. The success of both these games, as well as earlier titles, led to a publishing agreement between Take-Two and <a href="/wiki/Acclaim_Entertainment" title="Acclaim Entertainment">Acclaim Entertainment</a> to publish Take-Two's titles, as well as obtaining overseas distribution. Take-Two also secured a license with <a href="/wiki/Sony_Computer_Entertainment" class="mw-redirect" title="Sony Computer Entertainment">Sony Computer Entertainment</a> to publish on the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation" title="PlayStation">PlayStation</a> line of consoles.<sup id="cite_ref-Histories_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Histories-5">[5]</a></sup></p><p>Around 1996, the company was making about <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$10 million</span>, but Brant wanted to further expand the company, and made its first acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Mission_Studios" class="mw-redirect" title="Mission Studios">Mission Studios</a> and publishing its <i><a href="/wiki/JetFighter_III" class="mw-redirect" title="JetFighter III">JetFighter III</a></i> game in 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-The_End_Game_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_End_Game-6">[6]</a></sup> Brant decided to secure additional funds for acquisition by taking the company public. The company completed its <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">initial public offering</a> (IPO) on April 15, 1997, being listed under the <a href="/wiki/Ticker_symbol" title="Ticker symbol">ticker symbol</a> <b>TTWO</b> on the <a href="/wiki/NASDAQ" class="mw-redirect" title="NASDAQ">NASDAQ</a> stock exchange.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> From the IPO, the company gained about <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$6.5 million</span> along with <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$4 million</span> on venture fund promissory notes.<sup id="cite_ref-Histories_5-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Histories-5">[5]</a></sup> The additional funds allowed Take-Two to acquire <a href="/wiki/GameTek" title="GameTek">GameTek</a>'s European operations, their internal <a href="/wiki/Alternative_Reality_Technologies" class="mw-redirect" title="Alternative Reality Technologies">Alternative Reality Technologies</a> studio (later renamed Rockstar Toronto), and the distribution rights to GameTek's <i>Dark Colony</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Jeopardy!_(video_game)" class="mw-redirect" title="Jeopardy! (video game)">Jeopardy!</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Wheel_of_Fortune_(video_game)" class="mw-redirect" title="Wheel of Fortune (video game)">Wheel of Fortune</a></i> games.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> Additionally, the company acquired Inventory Management Systems, Creative Alliance Group, and Alliance Inventory Management, three video game distribution companies that helped to extend Take-Two's reach into the retail market.<sup id="cite_ref-Histories_5-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Histories-5">[5]</a></sup></p><p>In March 1998, Take-Two acquired BMG Interactive, the dormant video game publishing division of <a href="/wiki/Bertelsmann_Music_Group" title="Bertelsmann Music Group">BMG Entertainment</a>, for 1.85 million shares (16% of Take-Two's <a href="/wiki/Common_stock" title="Common stock">common stock</a>), worth about <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$14.2 million</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> In the previous year, the United Kingdom-based <a href="/wiki/DMA_Design" class="mw-redirect" title="DMA Design">DMA Design</a> and BMG Entertainment had just released <i><a href="/wiki/Grand_Theft_Auto_(video_game)" title="Grand Theft Auto (video game)">Grand Theft Auto</a></i>, and while it financially performed well but was not a critical success in Europe, it had sparked controversy over the use of violence in video games, with United States Senator <a href="/wiki/Joe_Lieberman" title="Joe Lieberman">Joe Lieberman</a> speaking out strongly against it. Seeing the opportunity to capture attention on the game, Brant had initiated the acquisition of BMG as to acquire the <i>Grand Theft Auto</i> property, and at the same time, contacted BMG's <a href="/wiki/Sam_Houser" title="Sam Houser">Sam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dan_Houser" title="Dan Houser">Dan Houser</a> (both instrumental to getting <i>Grand Theft Auto</i> to market), Terry Donovan, and Jamie King to found a new label within Take-Two, called <a href="/wiki/Rockstar_Games" title="Rockstar Games">Rockstar Games</a> for which to develop more titles like it.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Arts" title="Electronic Arts">Electronic Arts</a>' (EA) 2008 CEO, <a href="/wiki/John_Riccitiello" title="John Riccitiello">John Riccitiello</a>, stated that, with the establishing of Rockstar, Take-Two effectively invented the "label" corporate structure, which EA followed into in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> With the rights to <i>Grand Theft Auto</i>, Take-Two expanded its publication into North America, and the game became Take-Two's first financial success with over 1.5 million copies sold.<sup id="cite_ref-Histories_5-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Histories-5">[5]</a></sup></p><p>Take-Two also began taking on distribution capabilities, acquiring various distribution firms such as DirectSoft Australia for the Oceania market.<sup id="cite_ref-Histories_5-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Histories-5">[5]</a></sup> Notably, in August 1998, Take-Two acquired <a href="/wiki/Jack_of_All_Games" title="Jack of All Games">Jack of All Games</a>, an America game distributor, for about <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$16.8 million</span>. Take-Two subsequently bundled many of its existing and future distribution outlets under the Jack of All Games brand.<sup id="cite_ref-Distributor_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Distributor-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p><p>In 1999, Take-Two acquired DMA Design (ultimately renamed <a href="/wiki/Rockstar_North" title="Rockstar North">Rockstar North</a>), and invested into <a href="/wiki/Gathering_of_Developers" title="Gathering of Developers">Gathering of Developers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bungie" title="Bungie">Bungie</a> (eventually transferred over to <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Game_Studios" class="mw-redirect" title="Microsoft Game Studios">Microsoft Game Studios</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Histories_5-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Histories-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> In September, the company also acquired Triad Distributors and Global Star Software, a video game distributor and publisher, respectively, both founded in 1993 by Craig McGauley and Damian Cristiani and operating out of the same offices in <a href="/wiki/Concord,_Ontario" title="Concord, Ontario">Concord, Ontario</a>, with the same management team.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="2001.E2.80.932006:_Further_acquisitions_and_regulatory_investigations"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2001–2006:_Further_acquisitions_and_regulatory_investigations">2001–2006: Further acquisitions and regulatory investigations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Take-Two_Interactive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 2001–2006: Further acquisitions and regulatory investigations" data-section="3" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>With Rockstar, Take-Two invested into developments of sequels to <i>Grand Theft Auto</i>, including <i><a href="/wiki/Grand_Theft_Auto_2" title="Grand Theft Auto 2">Grand Theft Auto 2</a></i> (1999), and <i><a href="/wiki/Grand_Theft_Auto_III" title="Grand Theft Auto III">Grand Theft Auto III</a></i> (2001) along with spin-outs, <i><a href="/wiki/Grand_Theft_Auto:_Vice_City" title="Grand Theft Auto: Vice City">Grand Theft Auto: Vice City</a></i> (2003) and <i><a href="/wiki/Grand_Theft_Auto:_San_Andreas" title="Grand Theft Auto: San Andreas">Grand Theft Auto: San Andreas</a></i> (2004). By 2003, Take-Two had revenues exceeding <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$1 billion</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> In 2004, Take-Two paid <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$22.3 million</span> to <a href="/wiki/Infogrames" class="mw-redirect" title="Infogrames">Infogrames</a> for the rights to the <a href="/wiki/Civilization_(series)" title="Civilization (series)"><i>Civilization</i> series</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p><p>In 2005, Take-Two began a host of acquisitions, spending more than <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$80 million</span> buying game developers.<sup id="cite_ref-Hot_Coffee_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hot_Coffee-23">[23]</a></sup> One of its largest acquisitions was for the development studios <a href="/wiki/Visual_Concepts" title="Visual Concepts">Visual Concepts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kush_Games" class="mw-redirect" title="Kush Games">Kush Games</a> from <a href="/wiki/Sega" title="Sega">Sega</a> for about <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$32 million</span> in January 2005. Both studios had been extensively behind several sports simulation games, branded through <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a>, and typically released updated versions each year, using a <i>2K</i> brand to differentiate versions (such as <i><a href="/wiki/ESPN_NFL_2K5" title="ESPN NFL 2K5">ESPN NFL 2K5</a></i>). In 2004, Take-Two had struck a deal with Sega to help publish these titles. Just prior to Take-Two's acquisition, <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Arts" title="Electronic Arts">Electronic Arts</a> announced it had secured the exclusive rights to create video games based on the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a> (NFL) and a fifteen-year branding deal with <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a>, effectively killing Visual Concepts' own NFL title and devaluing their others games. This decision led Sega to abandon the sports-game market. Take-Two acquired these studios and unique branding (including the <i>2K</i> brand), as well as negotiated for exclusive rights with <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> for video games.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> A day after announcing these acquisitions, Take-Two established their <a href="/wiki/2K_(company)" title="2K (company)">2K</a> publishing label to maintain the <i>2K</i> brand, moving several planned games from their budget software label, Global Star, to 2K. Take-Two further realigned the other existing internal studios — Indie Built, Venom Games, PopTop Software and Frog City Software, and Take-Two Licensing — within this new structure.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p><p>After the formation of 2K, Take-Two completed other major acquisitions. <a href="/wiki/Firaxis_Games" title="Firaxis Games">Firaxis Games</a> was acquired in November 2005 for around <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$27 million</span>;<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Take-Two had already supported the studio by using their acquisition of the <i>Civilization</i> license to support publishing of <i><a href="/wiki/Civilization_IV" title="Civilization IV">Civilization IV</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup>  <a href="/wiki/Irrational_Games" title="Irrational Games">Irrational Games</a> was acquired around January 2006 for about <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$10 million</span>, including both its Boston and its Canberra studio.<sup id="cite_ref-Hot_Coffee_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hot_Coffee-23">[23]</a></sup> At the time Irrational had already established a publishing deal with Take-Two for their upcoming <i><a href="/wiki/BioShock" title="BioShock">BioShock</a></i> game. With the deal, Irrational became part of the 2K label.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> It also acquired PAM Development from the Gaia Capital Group for <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$11.4 million</span>, giving them access to the <i><a href="/wiki/Top_Spin_(video_game)" title="Top Spin (video game)">Top Spin</a></i> series of tennis games.<sup id="cite_ref-Hot_Coffee_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hot_Coffee-23">[23]</a></sup></p><p>However, during this period, the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Securities_and_Exchange_Commission" title="U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission">U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission</a> (SEC) had begun examining Take-Two's business records, based on complaints filed from 2001 that Take-Two's earnings did not seem to match figures of game sales reported by <a href="/wiki/NPD_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="NPD Group">NPD Group</a>. The SEC's formal complaint found the company had purported sold product to distributors as a "parking transaction" for a quarter, as to artificially increase their revenues for investors, which it estimated was a <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$60 million</span> fraud.<sup id="cite_ref-Guilty_Plea_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guilty_Plea-30">[30]</a></sup> After SEC's issuance of the complaint in 2005, Take-Two agreed to pay the <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$7.5 million</span> fine, along with Brant and other executives paying fines totaling around <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$6.4 million</span>. However, prior to that, Brant had already stepped down as CEO to remain as chairman through 2004, after which he became Vice President of Production, as he had been barred by the SEC from serving as an officer or director of a publicly traded company. Brant ultimately resigned from the company in October 2006, following a four-month disability leave due to a bad back.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p><p>A separate investigation by the SEC found further issues with Brant and two other executives of the company in 2007. In an industry-wide sweep against <a href="/wiki/Options_backdating" title="Options backdating">options backdating</a> (receiving shares when they are priced high but backdating their ownership to when they were priced low), the SEC had found Brant had received backdating options of over 2.1 million shares, though he had excised all options upon his 2006 resignation. Brant pleaded guilty to falsifying business records, but agreed to cooperate with the SEC and instead of receiving up to four years in prison, was fined <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$7.3 million</span> and barred from holding any "control management positions" in a publicly traded company.<sup id="cite_ref-Guilty_Plea_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guilty_Plea-30">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Brant ultimately died in March 2019 at the age of 49.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p><p>Further troubling Take-Two during this period was criticism and legal actions taken against the <a href="/wiki/Hot_Coffee_mod" title="Hot Coffee mod"><i>Hot Coffee</i> mod</a>, a user-made <a href="/wiki/Mod_(video_gaming)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mod (video gaming)">modification</a> to <i>Grand Theft Auto: San Andreas</i> that unlocked a hidden graphic sex scene that was built into the game, with concerned politicians and consumers stating the scene belied the game's <a href="/wiki/ESRB" class="mw-redirect" title="ESRB">ESRB</a> content rating.  Among actions taken against Take-Two included an investigation by the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Trade_Commission" title="Federal Trade Commission">Federal Trade Commission</a> for deceptive advertising, to which Take-Two and Rockstar settled in 2006 on fines for any future violations of content ratings.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Take-Two completed a <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$20.1 million</span> settlement related to class-action lawsuits filed against it in 2005 over the <i>Hot Coffee</i> mod, as well as to a class-action lawsuit brought by shareholders over the options backdating fraud, in September 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="2007.E2.80.932008:_Shareholder_takeover_and_attempted_buy-out"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2007–2008:_Shareholder_takeover_and_attempted_buy-out">2007–2008: Shareholder takeover and attempted buy-out</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Take-Two_Interactive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2007–2008: Shareholder takeover and attempted buy-out" data-section="4" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>A fire had damaged part of the Take-Two headquarters building in New York in 2006. In early January 2007, Take-Two relocated the headquarters for 2K to <a href="/wiki/Novato,_California" title="Novato, California">Novato, California</a> to 65,000 square feet of space at Hamilton Landing, an office park that had repurposed the former hangar structures from the <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_Army_Airfield" title="Hamilton Army Airfield">Hamilton Army Airfield</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Later that year in September, Take-Two established a partnership with <a href="/wiki/Nickelodeon" title="Nickelodeon">Nickelodeon</a> and launched a new label, <a href="/wiki/2K_Play" class="mw-redirect" title="2K Play">2K Play</a>, designed for publishing of family-friendly titles alongside 2K's 2K Games and 2K Sports sub-labels, absorbing the remaining publishing duties of the Global Star label.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> In December 2007, Take-Two established <a href="/wiki/2K_Marin" title="2K Marin">2K Marin</a> (named after <a href="/wiki/Marin_County,_California" title="Marin County, California">Marin County</a>, where Novato is located) and expanded its presence at Hamilton Landing.<sup id="cite_ref-Alexander_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alexander-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Strauss_Zelnick,_2015_(16339090774).jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Strauss_Zelnick%2C_2015_%2816339090774%29.jpg/150px-Strauss_Zelnick%2C_2015_%2816339090774%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="225" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1368" data-file-height="2048"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 150px;height: 225px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Strauss_Zelnick%2C_2015_%2816339090774%29.jpg/150px-Strauss_Zelnick%2C_2015_%2816339090774%29.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="150" data-height="225" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Strauss_Zelnick,_2015_(16339090774).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Zelnick in 2015</div></div></div>
<p>Due to the various SEC investigations and the <i>Hot Coffee</i> controversy, investors in Take-Two discussed the possibility to taking over the company at its next board meeting in March 2007, as to oust the company's current management. There was also issues with Take-Two failing to make its revenue targets, having lost <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$163.3 million</span> in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-Stockholders_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stockholders-40">[40]</a></sup> The investors, OppenheimerFunds Inc., S.A.C. Capital Management, Tudor Investment Corp., D.E. Shaw Valence Portfolios and <a href="/wiki/ZelnickMedia" class="mw-redirect" title="ZelnickMedia">ZelnickMedia</a>, held 46% of the company's stock at this point, and were looking to put ZelnickMedia's <a href="/wiki/Strauss_Zelnick" title="Strauss Zelnick">Strauss Zelnick</a> as the chairman of the board while outing long-standing management and board members. Zelnick had previously been president and CEO of BMG's North American division at the time of the sale of BMG Interactive to Take-Two, a move he had been against believing that BMG could have capitalized on the video game sector more. Following BMG, Zelnick had been COO of <a href="/wiki/20th_Century_Fox" class="mw-redirect" title="20th Century Fox">20th Century Fox</a> and CEO of <a href="/wiki/Crystal_Dynamics" title="Crystal Dynamics">Crystal Dynamics</a>. He founded ZelnickMedia few years later in 2001 as a private equity firm to focus on media and interactive entertainment investments.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Industry analyst <a href="/wiki/Michael_Pachter" title="Michael Pachter">Michael Pachter</a> stated that a takeover would be best for Take-Two, as the present management "completely abdicated any responsibility for the oversight of the options-granting policy. A more responsible board would have committed hari-kari."<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> The current CEO, Paul Eibeler, who had replaced Brant after his resignation, had tried to find a buyer for Take-Two after the investors filed their intent with the SEC, among which included EA,<sup id="cite_ref-Riccitiello_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Riccitiello-43">[43]</a></sup> but could not negotiate a sale before the meeting. The takeover was successfully agreed to by stockholders on March 29, 2007, with Zelnick naming Ben Feder, a partner at ZelnickMedia, as the new CEO.<sup id="cite_ref-Stockholders_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stockholders-40">[40]</a></sup> As of July 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Take-Two_Interactive&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Strauss Zelnick is the largest single shareholder by voting power.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p><p>The company announced a major restructuring in mid-2007, following the takeover. With the move of the 2K labels to Novato, the executive, management, distribution and sales areas were evaluated to align these by business discipline rather than geography.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Subsequently, the company let go about 5 to 15% of its approximately 2100 employees, closed down some of its European offices and centralizing these in its Geneva location, and looked to get out of the distribution market by looking for buyers of Jack of All Games.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p><p>In mid-February 2008, EA made a <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$25</span>-per-share all-cash transaction offer worth around <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$1.9 billion</span><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> to the board of Take-Two, subsequently revising it to <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$26</span> per share after being rejected and making the offer known to the public.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> At the time, Take-Two's stock was valued around <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$10</span> per share.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> EA CEO <a href="/wiki/John_Riccitiello" title="John Riccitiello">John Riccitiello</a> said that EA had previous considered a deal for Take-Two in the previous year when they were approached by Eibeler,<sup id="cite_ref-Riccitiello_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Riccitiello-43">[43]</a></sup> however, with <a href="/wiki/Activision" title="Activision">Activision</a>'s acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Vivendi_Games" title="Vivendi Games">Vivendi Games</a> in December 2007, EA was looking resecure itself as one of the top video game publishers with the acquisition of Take-Two. While Take-Two had been discussing the potential of a buyout to a large media company after the shareholder takeover, Zelnick and the board rejected the offer, with Zelnick stating "We didn't slam the door, we just said look, the price is not right and the time is wrong".<sup id="cite_ref-1.9_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1.9-51">[51]</a></sup> Take-Two offered to discuss the offer after <i><a href="/wiki/Grand_Theft_Auto_IV" title="Grand Theft Auto IV">Grand Theft Auto IV</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'s</span> release on April 29, 2008, which many considered to be the lucrative property that EA desired.<sup id="cite_ref-1.9_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1.9-51">[51]</a></sup> An acquisition would have ended EA's main competition in sports video games.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> EA continued to extend its bid offer throughout 2008, but by September 2008, EA decided to back away and let the offer expire, as Take-Two continued to call EA's cash offer as inadequate.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="2008.E2.80.93present:_Continued_growth"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2008–present:_Continued_growth">2008–present: Continued growth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Take-Two_Interactive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2008–present: Continued growth" data-section="5" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In September 2008, Take-Two established an outsourcing agreement with Ditan Distribution LLC, at the time owned by <a href="/wiki/Cinram" title="Cinram">Cinram</a>, a Canadian manufacturer of optical media. Through the agreement, Take-Two offloaded all distributing duties from Jack of All Games to Ditan, while establishing the means for Jack of All Games to license and distribute third-party titles.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Subsequently, in December 2009, Take-Two sold Jack of All Games to <a href="/wiki/Synnex" title="Synnex">Synnex</a> for about <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$43 million</span>, leaving the distribution market and focusing solely on development and publishing.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p><p>In 2010, Ben Feder stepped down as CEO, and was replaced by Zelnick, who remains the company's chairman and CEO.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> In January 2013, while being dissolved, <a href="/wiki/THQ" title="THQ">THQ</a> sold the rights of the <i>WWE</i> wrestling games series to Take-Two.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Subsequently, 2K Sports has published annual <i>WWE 2K</i> games as part of its lineup.
</p><p>Around 2013, Take-Two began to <a href="/wiki/Share_repurchase" title="Share repurchase">repurchase</a> about 7.5 million outstanding shares of the company (about 10%), based on the company's projections that it would remain profitable over the next several years. As part of this, the company bought back around 12 million shares owned by <a href="/wiki/Carl_Icahn" title="Carl Icahn">Carl Icahn</a>, about 11% of the total shares, for about <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$203 million</span>. Icahn had been seen as favoring selling the company to a buyer. This subsequently led to three board members who had been recommended on the board by Icahn to resign.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> The move to buy back shares was seen by analysts of the company's assurance in <i><a href="/wiki/Grand_Theft_Auto_V" title="Grand Theft Auto V">Grand Theft Auto V</a></i>, which was released in September 2013. <i>Grand Theft Auto V</i> has since sold nearly 100 million units by 2018, making it one of the most successful video games ever and bringing an estimated <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$6 billion</span> to Take-Two, increasing its stock value by more than 600%.<sup id="cite_ref-motleyfool_2018_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-motleyfool_2018-59">[59]</a></sup></p><p>On December 2013, former <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Comics" title="Marvel Comics">Marvel</a> editor-in-chief <a href="/wiki/Bill_Jemas" title="Bill Jemas">Bill Jemas</a> announced that he had joined Take-Two to start a "graphic fiction imprint".<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> The imprint, <a href="/wiki/Double_Take_Comics" title="Double Take Comics">Double Take Comics</a>, was launched in October 2014,<sup id="cite_ref-Double_Take_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Double_Take-61">[61]</a></sup> but ultimately was not successful and was shuttered in November 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-combined_universe_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-combined_universe-62">[62]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Leslie_Benzies" title="Leslie Benzies">Leslie Benzies</a>, former President of Rockstar North, took <a href="/wiki/Sabbatical" title="Sabbatical">sabbatical</a> leave from Rockstar on September 1, 2014. In January 2016 it was announced that he had left the company.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> On April 12, 2016, Benzies started legal action against Rockstar and Take-Two claiming $150 million in unpaid royalties.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Take-Two had invested into mobile-game developer <a href="/wiki/Scopely" title="Scopely">Scopely</a> in July 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> On February 1, 2017, the company acquired social and mobile game developer <a href="/wiki/Social_Point" class="mw-redirect" title="Social Point">Social Point</a> for about <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$250 million</span> to enter into the mobile gaming industry.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p><p>In that same month, Take-Two and the <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">National Basketball Association</a> (NBA) announced a partnership to create the <a href="/wiki/NBA_2K_League" title="NBA 2K League">NBA 2K League</a>, a profession eSports league based on the <i><a href="/wiki/NBA_2K" title="NBA 2K">NBA 2K</a></i> games, and the first eSports league to be managed by a professional sports league. Teams for the League are to be partially sponsored by existing NBA teams, so that there would be eSports equivalent teams for each of the thirty professional NBA teams. The inaugural season is planned to launch in May 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p><p>On May 31, 2017, Take-Two Interactive acquired <i><a href="/wiki/Kerbal_Space_Program" title="Kerbal Space Program">Kerbal Space Program</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> Later, Take-Two announced the formation of its <a href="/wiki/Private_Division" title="Private Division">Private Division</a> publishing label on December 14, 2017. Private Division was established to fund and publish games by mid-size independent development studios, such as <i>Kerbal Space Program</i>, and had four planned games from separate studios at its launch.<sup id="cite_ref-Private_Division_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Private_Division-71">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p><p>The company completed its move of its New York headquarters from <a href="/wiki/NoHo" class="mw-redirect" title="NoHo">NoHo</a> to more than 61,000 square feet of space in <a href="/wiki/Bryant_Park" title="Bryant Park">Bryant Park</a> in early 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Dan_Houser" title="Dan Houser">Dan Houser</a>, Rockstar Games required to expand in the two companies' shared headquarters and thus asked the Take-Two executives to move.<sup id="cite_ref-Goldberg_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Goldberg-74">[74]</a></sup> On March 8, 2018, Zelnick attended a White House meeting held by the 45th President of the United States, <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>, along with various other attendees involved with the video game industry, and members of Congress, to discuss video game violence in the wake of the <a href="/wiki/Stoneman_Douglas_High_School_shooting" title="Stoneman Douglas High School shooting">Stoneman Douglas High School shooting</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p><p>On March 9, 2018, <a href="/wiki/S%26P_Global" title="S&amp;P Global">S&amp;P Global</a> announced the addition of Take-Two Interactive to the <a href="/wiki/S%26P_500" class="mw-redirect" title="S&amp;P 500">S&amp;P 500</a>, joining two other major video game publishers EA and <a href="/wiki/Activision_Blizzard" title="Activision Blizzard">Activision Blizzard</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> Similar to the situation in 2013, Take-Two started buying back around <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$308 million</span> of its stock (estimated to be about 2.5% of the outstanding stock), predicated on similar expectations that <i><a href="/wiki/Red_Dead_Redemption_2" title="Red Dead Redemption 2">Red Dead Redemption 2</a></i>, to be released in October 2018, would similarly boost the company's profits as <i>Grand Theft Auto V</i> had done.<sup id="cite_ref-motleyfool_2018_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-motleyfool_2018-59">[59]</a></sup></p><p>On March 29, 2018, Benzies' litigation against Rockstar and Take-Two suffered a significant setback when the companies succeeded in dismissing 12 out of 18 of his claims, though the court did rule that Benzies "remains entitled to receive certain royalties" as part of his compensation.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p><p>Sometime in 2018, Take-Two levied a legal warning against Benzies' new company Royal Circus Games, citing the similarity of its acronym (RCG) to Rockstar Games (RSG) as infringement of intellectual property; due to this, Benzies later renamed his company Build a Rocket Boy Games in October 2018. Take-Two had also decried their employment of Rockstar North staff as a deceptive tactic to create an affiliation between them.<sup id="cite_ref-McLaughlin-Jan2019_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McLaughlin-Jan2019-80">[80]</a></sup></p><p>Take-Two and the NBA signed a seven-year, <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$1.1 billion</span> licensing deal to extend Take-Two's rights to develop the <i>NBA 2K</i> games in January 2019. Analysts estimated that this represented at least 15% of Take-Two's revenue from the sale of <i>NBA 2K</i> games, atypical of other license deals, due to the growing popularity of the series.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p><p>A yet-named studio under the 2K brand in the <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Valley" title="Silicon Valley">Silicon Valley</a> region of the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay_Area" title="San Francisco Bay Area">San Francisco Bay Area</a> was established by Take-Two in February 2019. The studio will be led by <a href="/wiki/Michael_Condrey" title="Michael Condrey">Michael Condrey</a>, formerly of <a href="/wiki/Sledgehammer_Games" title="Sledgehammer Games">Sledgehammer Games</a> and <a href="/wiki/Visceral_Games" title="Visceral Games">Visceral Games</a>, and is working on an unannounced project.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p><p>On February 7, 2019, Benzies' litigation with Take-Two had officially come to an end.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> All parties involved in the case successfully executed a confidential settlement, with each agreeing to bear its own costs and expenses, including, without limitation, attorney's fees.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p><p>In May 2019, Rockstar Games announced that they had acquired <a href="/wiki/Dhruva_Interactive" title="Dhruva Interactive">Dhruva Interactive</a> from <a href="/wiki/Starbreeze_Studios" title="Starbreeze Studios">Starbreeze Studios</a> for $7.9 million, with the sale having been finalized later that same month. The company had been merged into <a href="/wiki/Rockstar_India" title="Rockstar India">Rockstar India</a>, which added an additional 320 employees to the studio.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p><p>In September 2019, Rockstar Games announced that they had released their own game launcher, a <a href="/wiki/Digital_distribution" title="Digital distribution">digital distribution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Digital_rights_management" title="Digital rights management">digital rights management</a>, <a href="/wiki/Multiplayer_video_game" title="Multiplayer video game">multiplayer</a> and communications service.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p><p>Take-Two established a new, yet-named studio under Private Division in February 2020 located in Seattle to take on the development of <i><a href="/wiki/Kerbal_Space_Program_2" class="mw-redirect" title="Kerbal Space Program 2">Kerbal Space Program 2</a></i>. The new studio staff included Jeremy Ables and Nate Simpson from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Theory&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Star Theory (page does not exist)">Star Theory</a>, which had been previously handling the development of the game but outside of Take-Two's structure.<sup id="cite_ref-new_ksp2_studio_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-new_ksp2_studio-89">[89]</a></sup></p><p>Via 2K Sports, Take-Two established a new publishing agreement with the NFL in March 2020 to start republishing NFL games starting in 2021. While EA's <i>Madden</i> series will coexist and remain the official game of the NFL, while 2K's are called "non-simulation football game experiences" to distinguish from EA's games.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Company_structure">Company structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Take-Two_Interactive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Company structure" data-section="6" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">
<p>Take-Two's executive offices and worldwide headquarters are located in New York City. The company runs its European operations from <a href="/wiki/Windsor,_Berkshire" title="Windsor, Berkshire">Windsor, England</a> and its Asian operations from <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>. As of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Take-Two_Interactive&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Take-Two's primary business is through two self-owned publishing labels. One label is <a href="/wiki/Rockstar_Games" title="Rockstar Games">Rockstar Games</a>, also located in New York City, and is specialized on development and publication of <a href="/wiki/Action-adventure_games" class="mw-redirect" title="Action-adventure games">action-adventure games</a> such as <i>Grand Theft Auto</i>. The other label is <a href="/wiki/2K_(company)" title="2K (company)">2K</a>, headquartered in Novato, California, and is composed of its divisions <a href="/wiki/2K_Games" class="mw-redirect" title="2K Games">2K Games</a>, <a href="/wiki/2K_Sports" class="mw-redirect" title="2K Sports">2K Sports</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2K_Play" class="mw-redirect" title="2K Play">2K Play</a>. The 2K Sports division handles the development and publication of Take-Two's sports simulation games, such as the <i><a href="/wiki/NBA_2K" title="NBA 2K">NBA 2K</a></i> series. 2K Play covers family-friendly and children's video games produced by Take-Two's studios. 2K Games handles nearly all other production from Take-Two's internal development studios as well as titles from selected third parties (such as the <i><a href="/wiki/Borderlands_(series)" title="Borderlands (series)">Borderlands</a></i> series developed by <a href="/wiki/Gearbox_Software" title="Gearbox Software">Gearbox Software</a>).
</p><p>Separately, Take-Two owns <a href="/wiki/Private_Division" title="Private Division">Private Division</a>, a label designed to help publish and market games from mid-sized independent developers, such as <a href="/wiki/Squad_(company)" title="Squad (company)">Squad</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Kerbal_Space_Program" title="Kerbal Space Program">Kerbal Space Program</a></i>. Finally, Take-Two owns <a href="/wiki/Social_Point" class="mw-redirect" title="Social Point">Social Point</a>, a developer for the <a href="/wiki/Mobile_game" title="Mobile game">mobile game</a> market. With this structure been in place since 1997–1998, each labels are incorporated principal operating businesses and have a higher degree of autonomy and each with their own infrastructure and resources, management, and profit and loss strategies.
</p><p>Take-Two has divested itself of its older manufacturing and distribution operations in favor of digital publication and third-party retail distribution. Since 2016, around half of the company's revenues are from digital distribution, whether from digital sales of games through personal computer or consoles, or through <a href="/wiki/Video_game_monetization" title="Video game monetization">video game monetization</a> of its computer, console, and mobile titles.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>

<td><sup id="cite_ref-The_End_Game_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_End_Game-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[154]</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_holdings">Other holdings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Take-Two_Interactive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Other holdings" data-section="11" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Take-Two equally shares control of the <a href="/wiki/NBA_2K_League" title="NBA 2K League">NBA 2K League</a>, a competitive esports league based on its <i><a href="/wiki/NBA_2K" title="NBA 2K">NBA 2K</a></i> series, along with the <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">National Basketball Association</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[155]</a></sup></p><p>The company has an undisclosed minority interest in <a href="/wiki/Scopely" title="Scopely">Scopely</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[156]</a></sup> It had previously held 19.9% interest in <a href="/wiki/Bungie" title="Bungie">Bungie</a>, which it turned over to <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Game_Studios" class="mw-redirect" title="Microsoft Game Studios">Microsoft Game Studios</a> on their acquisition in 2000, in exchange receiving the rights to Bungie's <i><a href="/wiki/Myth_(series)" title="Myth (series)">Myth</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Oni_(video_game)" title="Oni (video game)">Oni</a></i>, and two other games based on the <i><a href="/wiki/Halo_(video_game_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Halo (video game series)">Halo</a></i> engine.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[157]</a></sup> Take-Two also had a 2.3% interest in <a href="/wiki/Twitch_(service)" title="Twitch (service)">Twitch</a>, which was bought out upon the service's acquisition by <a href="/wiki/Amazon_(company)" title="Amazon (company)">Amazon</a> in 2014, receiving <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$22 million</span> from the sale.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[158]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(3)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Games_published">Games published</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Take-Two_Interactive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Games published" data-section="12" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-3 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-3">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Take-Two_Interactive_games" title="List of Take-Two Interactive games">List of Take-Two Interactive games</a></div>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(4)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Take-Two_Interactive&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Notes" data-section="13" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-4 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-4">
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references"><li id="cite_note-142"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-142">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">2K games had shut down 2K Marin entirely in 2013, but statements made by Zelnick in 2014 claimed 2K Marin would be responsible for future <i>BioShock</i> projects.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup>  With the opening of Cloud Chamber in December 2019, it is unclear what the fate of 2K Marin is.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
